shakespear there have be some age in which providence seem pleased in a most remarkable manner to display it self in give to the world the finest genius 's to illuminate a people formerly barbarous after a long night of gothic ignorance after many age of priestcraft and superstition learning and genius visit we island in the day of the renowned queen elizabeth it be then that liberty begin to dawn and the people have shake off the restraint of priestly austerity presume to think for themselves at a æra so remarkable as this so famous in history it seem no wonder that the nation would be bless with those immortal ornament of wit and learning who all conspire at once to make it famous -- this astonishing genius seem to be commission from above to deliver we not only from the ignorance under which we labor as to poetry but to carry poetry almost to its perfection but to write a panegyric on shakespear appear as unnecessary as the attempt would be vain for whoever have any taste for what be great terrible or tender may meet with the amplest gratification in shakespear as may those also have a taste for drollery and true humor he genius be almost boundless and he succeed alike in every part of write i can not forbear give the character of shakespear in the word of a great genius in a prologue speak by mr garrick when he first open drury-lane house as manager when learn 's triumph o'er she barb ` rous foe first rear have the stage -- immortal shakespear rise each change of many-coloured life he draw exhaust world and then imagine new existence see he spurn she bounded reign and panting time toil after he in vain all man have discover a curiosity to know the little story and particularity of a great genius for it often happen that when we attend a man to he closet and watch he moment of solitude we shall find such expression drop from he or we may observe such instance of peculiar conduct as will let we more into he real character than ever we can discover while we converse with he in public and when perhaps he appear under a kind of mask there be but few thing know of this great man few incident of he life have descend to posterity and tho ' no doubt the fame of he ability make a great noise in the age in which he flourish yet he station be not such as to produce many incident as it be subject to but few vicissitude mr rowe who well understand and greatly admire shakespear have be at pain to collect what incident be know or be to be find concern he and it be chiefly upon mr rowe 's authority we build the account now give we author be the son of john shakespear and be bear at stratford upon avon in warwickshire April 1564 at it appear by public record relate to that town the family from which he be descend be of good figure and fashion there and be mention as gentleman he father who be a considerable dealer in wool be incumbr with a large family of ten child could afford to give he eldest son but a slender education he have breed he at a free school where he acquire what latin he be master of but how well he understand that language or whether after he leave the school he make greater proficiency in it have be dispute and be a point very difficult to settle however it be certain that mr john shakespear we author 's father be oblige to withdraw he early from school in order to have he assistance in he own employment towards support the rest of the family it be without controversy say rowe that in he work we scarce find any trace that look like a imitation of the ancient the delicacy of he taste and the natural bent of he own great genius equal if not superior to some of the best of theirs would certainly have lead he to read and study they with so much pleasure that some of they fine image would naturally have insinuate themselves into and be mix with he own writings so that he not copy at least something from they may be a argument of he never have read they whether he ignorance of the ancient be disadvantageous to he or no may admit of dispute for tho ' the knowledge of they might have make he more correct yet it be not improbable but that the regularity and deference for they which would have attend that correctness might have restrain some of that fire impetuosity and even beautiful extravagance which we can not help admire in shakespear as to he want of learn mr pope make the follow just observation : that there be certainly a vast difference between learning and language how far he be ignorant of the latter i can not -lrb- say he -rrb- determine but it be plain he have much reading at least if they will not call it learn nor be it any great matter if a man have knowledge whether he have it from one language or from another nothing be more evident than that he have a taste for natural philosophy mechanic ancient and modern history poetical learning and mythology we find he very know in the custom rite and manners of the roman in coriolanus and julius cæsar not only the spirit but manners of the roman be exactly draw and still a nicer distinction be shewn between the manners of the roman in the time of the former and the latter he reading in the ancient historian be no less conspicuous in many reference to particular passage and the speech copy from plutarch in coriolanus may as well be make instance of he learning as those copy from cicero in the cataline of ben johnson the manners of other nation in general the ægyptians venetian french & c be draw with equal propriety whatever object of nature or branch of science he either speak or describe it be always with competent if not extensive knowledge he description be still exact and he metaphor appropriate and remarkably draw from the nature and inherent quality of each subject -- we have translation from ovid publish in he name among those poem which pass for he and for some of which we have undoubted authority be publish by himself and dedicate to the earl of southampton he appear also to have be conversant with plautus from whence he have take the plot of one of he play he follow the greek author and particularly dare phrygius in another although i will not pretend continue mr pope to say in what language he read they mr warburton have strongly contend for shakespear 's learning and have produce many imitation and parallel passage with ancient author in which i be incline to think he right and beg leave to produce few instance of it he always say mr warbur-ton make a ancient speak the language of a ancient so julius cæsar act i scene ii -- ye god it doth amaz I a man of such a feeble temper should so get the start of the majestic world and bear the palm alone this noble image be take from the olympic game this majestic world be a fine periphrasis of the roman empire majestic because the roman rank themselves on a footing with king and a world because they call they empire orbi romanus but the whole story seem to allude to cæsar 's great exemplar alexander who when he be ask whether he would run the course of the olympic game reply ` yes if the racer be king ' -- so again in anthony and cleopatra act i scene i anthony say with a astonishing sublimity difference between he and she brother war ` twixt you twain would be as if the world should cleave and that slay man should solder up the reft -- this thought seem take from the story of curtius leap into the chasm in the forum in order to close it so that as that be close by one roman if the whole world be to cleave roman only could solder it up the metaphor of soldering be extreamly exact accord \* \* \* beaumont and fletcher be two famous dramatist in the reign of jame i these two friend be so closely unite as author and be so jointly concern in the applause and censure bestow upon they play that it can not be think improper to connect they life under one article mr franci beaumont be descend from the ancient family of he name seat at grace dieu in leicestershire -lrb- 1 -rrb- and be bear about the year 1585 in the reign of queen elizabeth he grandfather john beaumont be master of the roll and he father franci beaumont one of the judge of the common plea we poet have he education at cambridge -lrb- 2 -rrb- but of what college we be not inform nor be it very material to know we find he afterwards admit a student in the inner-temple but we have no account of he make any proficiency in the law which be a circumstance attend almost all the poet who be breed to that profession which few man of sprightly genius care to be confine to before he be thirty year of age he die in 1615 and be bury the ninth of the same month in the entrance of st benedictine 's chapel within st peter 's westminster we meet with no inscription on he tomb but there be two epitaph writ on he one by he elder brother sir john beaumont and the other by bishop corbet that by he brother be pretty enough and be as follow : on death thy murderer this revenge i take : i slight he terror and just question make which of we two the best precedence have mine to this wretched world thine to the grave thou should ` st have follow I but death to blame miscounted year and measure age by fame so dearly hast thou buy thy precious line thy praise grow swiftly so thy life decline thy muse the hearer 's queen the reader 's love all ear all heart but death 's could please and move we poet leave behind he one the audience for want of judgment which in order to shew he versification i shall insert why should the man whose wit ne'er have a stain upon the public stage present he vein and make a thousand man brooke of beauchamps-court and one of the lord of the bed-chamber to he majesty this noble author be the friend of sir philip sidney than which a greater compliment can not be bestow as he be a poet and a man of wit he be hold in the highest esteem in that courtly age but he add to genius a gallantry of spirit and be as fine a soldier as a writer winstanley give a instance of he prowess in arm at the time -lrb- say he -rrb- when the french ambassador come over to england to negotiate a marriage between the duke of anjou and queen elizabeth for the better entertainment of the court solemn just be proclaim where the earl of arundel frederick lord windsor sir philip sidney and he be chief challenger against all comer in which challenge he behave himself so gallantly that he win the reputation of a most valiant knight thus you see that tho ' case be the nurse of poetry the muse be also companion to mar as may be exemplify in the character of the earl of surry sir philip sidney and sir fulk greville as we author loved and admire the lady it be somewhat extraordinary that he die a batchelor for in all that courtly age he could not find one on whom to confer the valuable prize of he heart as he be himself a learn man and possess a variety of knowledge so he patronize many necessitous candidate for fame but particularly camden whom he cause by he interest to be make king at arm he be likewise very liberal to mr speed the celebrated chronologer : find he a man of extensive knowledge and he occupation and circumstance mean so that he genius be depress by poverty he enable he to prosecute he study and pursue the bent of he genius without be oblige to drudge at a manual employment for he bread speed in he description of warwickshire write thus of lord brook whose merit -lrb- say he -rrb- towards I i do acknowledge in set my hand free from the daily employment of a manual trade and give it full liberty thus to express the inclination of mind himself be the procurer of my present estate he pass thro ' life in a calm of prosperity and honor beloved by he equal reverence by he inferior and a favorite at court but when he be about seventy year of age this life of undisturbed tranquility be sacrifice to the resentment of a villain and a catastrophe of the most tragical kind close the day of this worthy man one haywood who have be many year in he service and have behave with fidelity and honor expostulate with he freely -lrb- while they be alone -rrb- for he not have receive a due reward for he service he lordship enrage at he presumption and give way to he passion reprimand he very severely for he insolence for which the villain be now work up to the highest degree of fury take a opportunity to stab he with he dagger through the back into the vitals of which wound he instantly die September 30 1628 the murderer then strike with remorse horror and despair and all the natural attendant of he guilt retire to he chamber and have secure the door fall upon the same weapon with which he have assassinate he master and anticipate on himself the justice reserve for the hand of a executioner lord brooke be inter in warwickshire under a monument of black sum up he character in the word of mr cooper in she muse library as it be not easy to do it to better advantage i do not know -lrb- say she -rrb- whether a woman may be acquit for endeavor to sum up a character so various and important as he lordship 's but if the attempt can be excuse i do not desire to have it pass for a decisive sentence perhaps few man that deal in poetry have more learn or real wisdom than this nobleman and yet he stile be sometimes so dark and mysterious that one would imagine he choose rather to conceal than illustrate he meaning at other time he wit break out again with a uncommon brightness and shine i would almost say without a equal it be the same thing with he poetry sometimes so harsh and uncouth as if he have no ear for music at other so smooth and harmonious as if he be master of all its power the piece from which i shall quote some line be entitle a treatise of human learn the mind of man be this world 's true dimension and knowledge be the measure of the minde : and as the minde in she vast comprehension contain more world than all the world can finde so knowledge doth itself farre more extend than all the mind of man can comprehend a climb height it be without a head depth without bottome way without a end a circle with no line inviron not comprehend all it comprehend worth infinite yet satisfy no minde 'till it that infinite of \* \* \* \* \* sir walter raleigh be descend of a ancient family in devonshire which be seat in that county before the conquest -lrb- 1 -rrb- and be fourth son of walter raleigh esquire of fard in the parish of cornwood he be bear in the year 1552 at haye a pleasant farm of he father 's in the parish of budley in that part of devonshire border eastward upon the sea near where the ottery discharge itself into the british channel he be educate at the university of oxford where accord to dr fuller he become a commoner of oriel college as well as christ church and display in he early year a great vivacity of genius in he application to he study some have say that after leave the university he settle himself in the middle-temple and study the law but this opinion must be erroneous since he declare afterwards on he trial that he never read a word of law 'till he be prisoner in the tower in 1569 when he be not above 17 year of age he be one of the select troop of a hundred gentleman voluntier whom queen elizabeth permit henry champernon to transport into france for the assistance of protestant prince there -lrb- 2 -rrb- but of what service they be or what be the consequence of the expedition we have no account so great a scene of action as the whole kingdom of france be at that period give raleigh a opportunity of acquire experience and reading character as well as improve himself in the knowledge of language and manners and he own history of the world contain some remark which he then make of the conduct of some great general there of which he have himself be witness after we author 's return from france he embark in a expedition to the northern part of america with sir humphry gilbert he brother by the mother 's side that gentleman have obtain the queen 's patent to plant and inhabit such part of it as be unpossessed by any prince with whom she be in alliance but this attempt prove unsuccessful by means of the division which arise amongst the voluntier the next year 1580 upon the descent of the spanish and italian force in ireland under the pope 's banner for the support of the desmond in they rebellion in munster he have a captain 's commission under the lord gray of wilton to whom at that time the famous spenser be secretary but the chief service which captain raleigh perform be under thoma earl of ormond governor of munster he surprize the irish kern at ramile and have inclose they take every rebel upon the spot who do not fall in the conflict among the prisoner there be one laden with withy who be ask what he intend to have do with they boldly answer to have hang up the english charle upon which raleigh order he to be immediately dispatch in that manner and the rest of the robber and murderer to be punish accord to they desert -lrb- 3 -rrb- the earl of ormond depart for england in the spring of the year 1581 he government of munster be give to captain raleigh in which he behave with great vigilance and honor he fight the arch rebel barry at clove whom he charge with the utmost bravery and after a hard struggle put to flight in the month of August 1581 captain john gouch be appoint governor of munster by the lord deputy raleigh attend he in several journy to settle and compose that country but the chief place of they residence be cork and after gouch have cut off sir john desmond brother to the earl of desmond who be at the head of the rebellion he leave the government of that city to raleigh -lrb- 4 -rrb- whose company be not long after disband upon the reduction of that earl the slaughter of he brother and the submission of barry he return to england the lord deputy gray have resign the sword in ireland towards the end of August 1582 the dispute between he and raleigh upon reason which be variously assign by different writer be bring to a hearing before the council table in england where the latter support he cause with such ability as procured he the good opinion both of she majesty and the lord of the council and this add to the patronage of the earl of leicester be suppose to be one considerable occasion of he preferment though it do not immediately take place nor could the hope of it restrain he from a second expedition with he brother sir humphry gilbert to newfoundland for which he build a ship of 200 ton call the bark raleigh and furnish it compleatly for the voyage in which he resolve to attend he brother as he vice-admiral that fleet depart from plymouth the 11th of June 1583 but after it have be two or three day at sea a contagious distemper have seize the whole crew of raleigh 's ship oblige he to return to that port however by this accident he escape the misfortune of that expedition for after sir humphry have take possession of newfoundland in the right of the crown of england and assign land to every man of he company and fail three hundred league in the voyage home with full hope of the queen 's assistance to fit out a fleet next year he unfortunately perish for venture rashly in a frigate of but ten ton he be on the ninth of September that year at midnight swallow up in a high sea another vessel suffer the same fate and even the rest return not without great hazard and loss -lrb- 5 -rrb- : but this ill success could not divert raleigh from pursue a scheme of such importance to he country as those discovery in north america he draw up a account of the advantage of such a design and the means of prosecute it which he lay before the queen and council who be so well satisfy with the probability of success that on the 25th of march 1584 she majesty grant he letter patent in favor of he project contain free liberty to discover such remote heathen and barbarous land as be not actually possess by any christian prince nor inhabit by christian people immediately upon this grant raleigh choose two able and experienced captain and furnish they with two vessel fit out at he own expence with such expedition that on the 27th of April follow they set sail for the west of england take they course by the canary island where they arrive on the 10th of may towards the west indy and that be in those day the best and most frequented rout to america they pass by the carribbe island in the beginning of June and reach the gulph of florida on the 2d of July sailing along the shore about one hundred and twenty mile before they could find a convenient harbor at last they debark in a very low land which prove to be a island call wohoken and after take formal possession of the country they carry on a friendly correspondence with the native indian who supply they with a great variety of fish and venison and give they fur and deerskin in exchange for trifle thus encourage by the native eight of the company in a boat go up the river occam twenty mile and next day in the evening they come to a island call roanah which be but seven league from the place where they ship lay here they find the residence of the indian chief whose name be grangamineo whose house consist of nine apartment build of cedar fortify round with sharp piece of timber : he wife come out to they and order the people to carry they from the boat on they back and shew they many other civility they continue they intercourse with the native for some time still view the situation of the adjacent country and after have obtain the best information they could of the number and strength of the indian nation in that neighborhood and of they connexion alliance or contest with each other they return about the middle of September to england and make such a advantageous report of the fertility of the soil and healthiness of the climate that the queen favor the design of settle a colony in that country to which she be please to give the name of virginium -lrb- 6 -rrb- about two month after raleigh be choose knight of the shire for he county of devon and make a considerable figure in parliament where a bill pass in confirmation of he patent for the discovery of foreign country during the course of this session he receive the honor of knighthood from she majesty a distinction the more honorable to he as the queen be extreamly cautious in confer title and besides the patent for discovery she grant he about the same time a power to license the vend of wine throughout the kingdom which be in all probability very lucrative to he but it engage he in a dispute with the university of cambridge which have oppose one keymer whom he have license to sell wine there contrary to the privilege of that university the parliament be prorogue raleigh intent upon plant he new colony in virginia set out he own fleet of seven sail for that country under the command of he cousin sir richard greenville who after have visit the country leave behind he a hundred and seven person to settle a colony at roanah in he return to england he take a spanish prize worth 50000 l but this be not the only circumstance of good fortune which happen to raleigh this year for the rebellion in ireland be now suppress and the forfeit land divide into signiory among those principally who have be instrumental in the important service of reduce that country she majesty grant he one of the largest portion consist of twelve thousand acre in the county of cork and waterford with certain privilege and immunity upon condition of plant and improve the same to which the other grantee be oblige in the year 1586 we find we author so highly advance in the queen 's favor so extremely popular on account of he patronage of learn man ard the active spirit he exert in business that she majesty make he seneschal in the dutchy of cornwall but these distinction incur the usual effect of court preferment and expose sir walter to the envy of those who be much inferior to he in merit and even the earl of leicester himself who have formerly be he great patron become jealous of he and set up in opposition to he he nephew the young earl of essex the comedian likewise take the liberty to reflect upon raleigh 's power and influence upon the queen which she majesty resent so highly as to forbid tarleton the most celebrated actor of that age from approach she presence raleigh sollicitous for the prosperity of the plantation in virginium send out new supplies from time to time some of whom be oblige to return home and the general alarm spread over the nation on account of the spanish invasion throw all thing into disorder about the beginning of the year 1587 he be raise to the dignity of captain of she majesty 's guard which he hold together with the place of lord-warden of the stannary and lieutenant-general of the county of cornwall from this time till the year 1594 we find sir walter continually engage in project new expedition send succor to colony abroad or manage affair in parliament with consummate address in the year 1593 we find father parson the jesuit charge he with no less a crime than atheism and that he have found a school in which he teach atheistical principle and have make a great many young gentleman convert to they the most considerable authority to countenance the suspicion of sir walter 's religion be that of archbishop abbot who in a letter date at lambeth address to sir thoma roe then a ambassador at the mogul 's court expressly charge sir walter with doubt god 's be and omnipotence -lrb- 7 -rrb- but it be highly probable sir walter 's opinion might be misrepresent by he enemy or wrong conclusion draw from those which he maintain and it would be a shocking injustice to the memory of so great a man to suspect he of irreligion whose writings contain not the least trace of it and whose history of the world in particular breathe a strong spirit of real and genuine piety in the heighth of he favor with the queen he fall under she majesty 's displeasure for be enamour of mr elizabeth throgmorton one of the queen 's maid of honor whom he debauch and such it seem be the chastity of these time that a frailty of that sort be look upon as the highest offence she majesty be so exasperated that she command he to be confine several month and after he enlargement forbid he the court whence the poor lady be likewise dismiss from she attendance about the maiden queen who appear in this case the champion of virginity sir walter soon make she a honorable reparation by marriage and they be both example of conjugal affection and fidelity during the time we author continue under she majesty 's displeasure for this offence he project the discovery of the rich and extensive empire of guiana in the south of america which the spaniard have then visit and to that day have never conquer for this purpose have collect information relate to it he send a old officer to take a view of the coast who return the year follow with a very favourable account of the riches of the country which he have receive from some of the principal cassique upon the border of it this determine raleigh 's resolution who provide a squadron of ship at a very great expence and the lord high admiral howard and sir robert cecil conceive so good a opinion of the design that both concur in it he personally engage in the attempt and with no great number of ship so far explore the unknown country that he make greater progress in a few month than the spaniard have do for many year and have satisfy himself of the certainty of the gold mine of the country he return home with honor and riches the latter end of the summer 1595 and in the year follow publish in quarto a account of the voyage and discovery dedicate to lord admiral howard and sir robert cecil the next year sir walter be so far restore to the queen 's favor that he be engage in the important and successful expedition to cadiz in which the earl of essex and lord king sign the warrant for the execution of the lord cobham and gray and sir griffin markham at winchester pretend say lord cecil to forbear sir walter for the present till lord cobham 's death have to the tower of london with the rest of the prisoner of whom markham afterwards obtain he liberty and travel abroad lord gray of wilton die in the tower lord cobham be confine there many year during he old scheme of settle guiana which he have so much at heart that even during he imprisonment he hold a constant correspondence with that country send thither every year or every second year a ship to keep the indian in hope of be relieve from the tyranny of the spaniard who have again encroach upon they and massacre many both of the inhabitant and of raleigh 's man in these ship be bring several native of the country with whom he converse in the tower and obtain all possible information concern it upon such information he offer he scheme for prosecute he discovery to the court before he undertake it in person : nor be there any doubt either as to the improbability of the design or its unlawfulness notwithstanding the peace make with spain otherwise the king would not have make such grant as he do even at that time which shew that he be then convince that sir walter have in he first voyage discover and take possession of that country for the crown of england and consequently that he subject be justly intitle to any benefit that might arise from its discovery without the least respect to the pretension of the spaniard : besides when sir walter first move the court upon opinion when he grow so unreasonably fond of that match in 1616 he obtain a royal commission to settle guiana at the expence of himself and he friend he be appoint general and commander in chief of he the whole expence of this expedition be defray by raleigh and he friend the fleet consist of about seven sail on the 17th of November 1617 they come in sight of guiana and soon after to anchor in bear wise than make so by study he be admit commoner of harthall together with he younger brother in michaelmas term 1584 -lrb- 2 -rrb- by advice of he relation who be roman catholic he decline take the oath tender upon the occasion of take degree after he have study three year at the university he remove to cambridge and from thence three year after to lincoln 's - inn about this time he father die and leave he a portion of 3000 # he become soon distinguish at lincoln 's - inn by he rapid progress in the law he be now eighteen year of age and as yet have attach himself to no particular denomination of christian and as he relation be bigott to the romish faith he be induce to examine the controversy and to embrace publickly that which appear to he to be best support by the authority of the scripture he relinquish the study of the law and devoted himself entirely to that of the controvert point between the protestant and catholic which end in a thorough conviction of the truth of the reform religion in the year 1596 and 1597 mr donne attend the earl of essex in he expedition against cadiz and the azore island and stay some year in italy and spain and soon after he return to england he be make secretary to lord chancellor egerton this probably be intend by he lordship only as a introduction to a more dignified place for he frequently express a high opinion of he secretary 's ability and when he afterwards by the sollicitation of he lady part with he he observe that he be fitter to be a secretary to a monarch than to he when he be in the lord chancellor 's family he marry privately without the consent of she father the daughter of sir george more chancellor of the garter and lord lieutenant of the tower who so much resent he daughter 's marriage without he george 's hearing that he daughter have engage she heart to donne he remove she to he own house in surry and friend on both side endeavor to weaken they affection for each other but without success be so far reconcile to he daughter and son as not to deny he paternal blessing but would contribute nothing towards they support mr donne 's fortune be greatly diminish by the expence of travels law-suit and the generosity of he temper however he want be in a great measure prevent by the seasonable bounty of they kinsman sir franci wooley who entertain they several year at he house at pilford in surry where we author have several child bear to he during he residence at pilford he apply himself with great diligence and success to the study of the civil and canon law and be about this time as he wife 's portion or 20 # quarterly for they maintenance till it be all pay he be incorporate master of art in the university of oxford have before take the same degree at cambridge 1610 about two health strongly oppose he departure tell he that she divining soul boad some ill in he absence bur sir robert 's importunity be not to be resist and he at last consent to go with he mr walton give a that he earnestly desire mr donne to declare what have befall he in the short time of he absence to which he be not able to make a present answer but after a long and perplexed pause do at last say : i have see a dreadful vision since i see you i have see my wife pass twice by I through this room with she hair hang about she shoulder and a dead child in she arm to which sir robert reply sure sir you have sleep since you see I and this be the result of some melancholy dream which i desire you to forget for you be now awake to which mr donne 's reply be i can not be surer that i now live than himself this elderton be a famous comedian in those day and a facetious companion who have a great readiness at rhime compose many catch on love and wine which be then in great vogue among the giddy and volatile part of the town but he be not more celebrated for drollery than drinking so that he obtain the name of the bacchanalian buffoon the red-nosed ballad-maker & c and at last by the viii he father lose he estate under queen mary in whose reign he suffer imprisonment and at last enter into holy order and die about a month before we poet 's birth -lrb- 1 -rrb- who be bear at westminster say wood in the year 1574 he be first educate at a private school in the church of st martin 's in the field afterwards remove to westminster school where the famous camden be master he mother who marry a bricklayer to she second husband take he from school and oblige he to work at he father-in-law 's trade but be extremely averse to that employment he go into the low country where he distinguish himself by he bravery have in the view of the army kill a enemy and take the opima spolium from he upon he return to england he apply himself again to he former study and wood say he be admit into st john 's college in the university of cambridge though he continuance there seem to have be but short he have some time after this the misfortune to fight a duel and kill he adversary who only slightly wound he in the arm for this he be imprison and be cast for he life be near execution he antagonist he say have a sword ten inch longer than he own while he lay in prison a popish priest visit he who find he inclination quite disengage as to religion and therefore take the opportunity to impress he with a belief of the popish tenet he mind then naturally melancholy cloud with apprehension and the dread of execution be the more easily impose upon however such be the force of that impression that for twelve year after he have gain he liberty he continue in the catholic faith and at last turn protestant whether from conviction or fashion can not be determine but when the character of ben be consider probability will be upon the side of the latter for he take every occasion to ridicule religion in he play and make it he sport in conversation on he leave the university he enter himself into a obscure playhouse call the green curtain somewhere about shoreditch or clerkenwell he be first a actor and probably only a stroll one for decker in he satyromastix a play publish in 1602 and design as a reply to johnson 's poetaster ` reproach he with have leave the occupation of a mortar trader to turn actor and with have put up a supplication to be a poor journeyman player in which he would have continue but that he could not set a good face upon it and so be cashiered besides if we admit that satire to be build on fact we learn further that he perform the part of zuliman at the pari garden in southwark and amble by a play-waggon on the high-way and take mad jeronymo 's part to get service amongst the mimick -lrb- 2 -rrb- ' shakespear be say to have first introduce he to the world by recommend a play of he to the stage at the time when one of the player have reject he performance and tell he it would be of no service to they company -lrb- 3 -rrb- he first print dramatic performance be a comedy entitle every man in he humor act in the year 1598 who order they immediately to be imprison and they be in great danger of lose they ear and nose as a correction of they wantonness nor could the most partial have blame he majesty if the punishment have be inflict for surely to ridicule a country from which they sovereign have just come the place of he nativity and the kingdom of he illustrious forefather be a most daring insult upon they releasement from prison we poet give a entertainment to he friend among whom be camden and selden when he aged mother drink to he -lrb- 4 -rrb- and shew he a paper of poison which she have design if the sentence of punishment have be inflict to have mix with he drink after she have first take a potion of it herself upon the accession of charle i to the crown he write a petition to that prince that he soul live in a alley he have a pension from the city of london from several of the nobility and gentry and particularly from mr sutton the founder of the charterhouse -lrb- 5 -rrb- in he last hall in the county of kent descend of a very ancient family who distinguish themselves in the war between the scotch and english before the union of crown the father of sir henry wotton -lrb- accord to the account of the learn bishop walton -rrb- be twice marry and after the death of he second wife say the bishop ` he inclination though naturally averse to all contention yet necessitate he be to have several suit of law which take up much of he time he be by diver of he friend perswade to remarriage to whom he often answer that if he do put on a resolution to marry he seriously resolve to avoid three sort of person namely those that have child law suit be of he kindred : and yet follow he own law suit he meet in westminster hall with one mr morton the widow of a gentleman of kent who be engage in several suit in law and observe she comportment the time of she hearing one of she cause before the judge he could not but at the same time compassionate she condition and so affect she person that though there be in she a concurrence of all those accident against which he have so seriously resolve yet he affection grow so strong that he then resolve to sollicit she for a wife and do and obtain she ' by this lady he have we author who receive the rudiment of he education from he mother who be it seem a woman of taste and capable of inspiring he with a love of polite accomplishment when he become fit for a academical education he be place in new college in oxford in the beginning of the year 1584 where living in the condition of a gentleman commoner he contract a intimacy with sir richard baker afterwards a eminent historian sir henry do not long continue there but remove to queen 's college where say walton he make a great progress in logic and philosophy and write a tragedy for the use of that college call tarroredo walton tell we ` that this tragedy be so interwoven with sentence and for the exact personate those passion and humor he propose to represent he so perform that the gravest of the society declare that he have in a flight employment give a early and solid testimony of he future ability ' on the 8th of June say wood 1588 he as a member of queen 's college supplicate the venerable congregation of regent that he might be admit to the degree of bachelor of art which desire be grant conditionally that he should determine the lend follow but whether he be admit or do determine or take any degree do not appear in any of the university register though mr walton say that about the twentieth year of he age he proceed master of art and at that time read in latin three lecture de ocello during the time he be at the university and gain much upon mankind by the reputation of he ability he father for whom he have the highest veneration die and leave he a hundred mark a year to be pay out of one of he manor of great value walton proceed to relate a very astonishing circumstance concern the father of we author which as it be of the visionary sort the reader may credit or not as he please it be however too curious to be here omit especially as the learn prelate walton already mention have tell it with great earnestness as if he be persuade of its reality in the year 1553 nichola wotton dean of canterbury uncle to we author 's father be ambassador in france in the reign of queen mary dream that he nephew thoma wotton be dispose to be a party in a very hazardous project which if not suddenly prevent would issue in the loss of he life and the ruin of he family the dean who be persuade of the importance of he own dream be very uneasy but lest he should be think superstitious he resolve to conceal the circumstance and not to acquaint he nephew or any body else with it but dream the same a second time he determine to put something in execution in consequence of it he accordingly write to the queen to send for he nephew thoma wotton out of kent and that the lord of the council might examine he about some imaginary conspiracy so as to give color for he be commit to jail declare that he would acquaint she majesty with the true reason of he request when he should next be so happy to pay he duty to she the queen comply with the dean 's desire who at that time it seem have great influence with that bigotted princess about this time a marriage be conclude between the queen of england and philip king of spain which not a little disobliged some of the nobility who be jealous leave they country by such a match should be subject to the dominion of spain and they independent rights invade by that imperious monarch these suspicion produce a insurrection which be head by the duke of suffolk and sir thoma wyat who both lose they life in the attempt to prevent the match by seize the queen for the design be soon discover easily defeat and those two person with many more suffer on a scaffold between sir thoma wyat and the wotton 's family there have be a long intimacy and sir thoma have really win mr wotton over to he interest and have he not be prevent by imprisonment he afterwards declare that he would have join he friend in the insurrection and in all probability would have fall a sacrifice to the queen 's resentment and the votary of the spanish match after sir henry quit the university of oxford he travel into france germany and italy where he reside above nine year and return to he own country perfectly accomplish in all the polite improvement which man of sense acquire by travel and well acquaint with the temper and genius of the people with whom he have converse and the different policy of they government he be soon take notice of after he return and become secretary to the famous robert devereux earl of essex that unfortunate favorite whose story be never exhibit on the stage say mr addison without affect the heart in the most sensible manner with he lordship he continue in the character of secretary 'till the earl be apprehend for he mutinous behavior towards the queen and put upon he trial wotton who do not think it safe to continue in england after the fall of he master retire to florence become acquaint with the great duke of tuscany and rise so high in he favor that he be entrust by he to carry letter to jame vi king of scot under the name of octavio baldus in order to inform that king of a design against he life walton inform we that though queen elizabeth be never willing to declare she successor yet the king of scot be generally believe to be the person on whom the crown of england would devolve the queen decline very fast both through age and visible infirmity those that be of the romish persuasion in point of religion know that the death of the queen and establish she succession be the crisis for destroy or support the protestant religion in this nation do therefore improve all opportunity for prevent a protestant prince to succeed she and as the pope 's excommunication of queen elizabeth have both by the judgment and practice of the jesuited papist expose she to be warrantably destroy so about that time there be many endeavor first to excommunicate and then to shorten the life of king jame vi immediately after wotton 's return from rome to florence which be about a year before the death of queen elizabeth ferdinand the great duke have intercept certain letter which discover a design against the life of the king of scot the duke abhor the scheme of assassination and resolve to prevent it advise with he secretary vietta by what mean a caution should be give to the scotch prince vietta recommend wotton as a person of the highest ability of any englishman then at he court : mr wotton be send for by he friend vietta to the duke who after many profession of trust and friendship acquaint he with the secret and send he to scotland with letter to the king and such antidote against poison as till then the scot have be stranger to mr wotton have depart from the duke assume the name and language of a italian which he speak so fluently and with so little mixture of a foreign dialect that he could scarcely be distinguish from a native of italy and think it best to avoid the line of english intelligence and danger post into norway and through that country towards scotland where he find the king at stirl when he arrive there he use means by one of the gentleman of he majesty 's bed-chamber to procure a speedy and private audience of he majesty declare that the business which he be to negotiate be of such consequence as have excite the great duke of tuscany to enjoin he suddenly to leave he native country of italy to impart it to the king the king be inform of this after a little wonder mix with jealousy to hear of a italian ambassador or messenger appoint a private audience that evening when mr wotton come to the presence chamber he be desire to lay aside he long rapier and be enter find the king there with three or four scotch lord stand distant in several corner of the chamber at the sight of whom he make a stand and which the king observe bid he be bold and deliver he message and he would undertake for the secresy of all who be present upon this he deliver he message and letter to he majesty in italian which when the king have graciously receive after a little pause mr wotton stept up to the table and whisper to the king in he own language that he be a englishman request a more private conference with he majesty and that he might be conceal during he stay in that nation which be promise and really perform by the king all the time he remain at the scotch court he then return to the duke with a satisfactory account of he employment when king jame succeed to the throne of england he find among other of queen elizabeth 's officer sir edward wotton afterwards lord wotton comptroller of the houshold whom he ask one day ` whether he know one henry wotton who have spend much time in foreign travel ' sir edward reply that he know he well and that he be he brother the king then ask where he be and upon sir edward 's answering that he believe he would soon be at paris send for he say he majesty and when he come to england bid he repair privately to I sir edward after a little wonder ask he majesty whether he know he to which the king answer you must rest unsatisfied of that 'till you bring the gentleman to I not many month after this discourse sir edward bring he brother to attend the king who take he in he arm and bid he welcome under the mine of octavio baldus say that he be the most honest and therefore the best dissembler he ever meet with and see i know add the king you want neither learn travel nor experience and that i have have so real a testimony of you faithfulness and ability to manage a embassage i have send for you to declare my purpose which be to make use of you in that kind hereafter -lrb- 1 -rrb- but before he dismiss octavio baldus from he present attendance he restore he to he old name of henry wotton by which he then knight he not long after this king jame have resolve accord to he motto of beatus pacificus to have a friendship with he neighbouring kingdom of france and spain and also to enter into a alliance with the state of venice and for that purpose to send ambassador to those several state offer to sir henry he choice of which ever of these employment best suit he inclination who from the consideration of he own personal estate be small and the court of france and spain extreamly sumptuous so as to expose he to expence above he fortune make choice of venice a place of more retirement and where he could execute he embassy and at the same time indulge himself in the study of natural philosophy in that seat of the science where he be sure to meet with man accomplish in all the polite improvement as well as the more solid attainment of philosophy have inform the king that he choose to be send to venice he majesty settle a very considerable allowance upon he during he stay there he then take he leave and be accompany through france to venice say walton by gentleman of the best family and breed that this nation afford when sir henry wotton arrive at venice there subsist between the venetian and the pope a very warm contention which be prosecute by both party with equal fury the laity make many complaint against the two frequent practice of land be leave to the church without a licence from the state which increase the power of the clergy already too great and render they insolence insupportable in consequence of this the state make several injunction against lay-person dispose they land in that manner another cause of they quarrel be that the venetian have send to rome several article of complaint against two priest the abbot of nervesa and a canon of vicenza for commit such abominable crime as mr walton say it would be a shame to mention : they complaint meet with no redress and the detestable practice of these monster in holy order still continue they seize they person and commit they to prison the justice or injustice of such power exercise by the venetian produce debate between the republic and pope clement viii clement soon die pope paul the first a man of unbounded insolence and elate with he spiritual superiority let loose all he rage against the state he judge all resistance to be a diminution of he power and threaten excommunication to the whole state if a revocation be not instantly make which the venetian reject he proceed in menace and at last do excommunicate the duke the whole senate and all they dominion then he shut up the church charge the clergy to forbear sacred office to any of the venetian till they obedience should make they capable of absolution the contention be thus fomented till a report prevail that the venetian be turn protestant which be believe by many as the english embassador be so often in conference with the senate and that they have make all they proceedings know to the king of england who would support they should the pope presume to exercise any more oppression this circumstance make it appear plain enough to he holiness that he weaken he power by exceed it and be alarm lest a revolution should happen offer the venetian absolution upon very easy term which the republic still slight do at last obtain it by that which be scarce so much as a shew of desire it for eight year after sir henry wotton 's go into italy he stand very high in the king 's esteem but at last lose he favor for some time by a accident too singular to be here omit when he first go embassador to italy as he pass through germany he staid some day at augsburgh where have be in he former travels well know by many of the first reputation in learning and pass a evening in merriment he be desire by christopher hecamore to write a sentence in he album and consent to it take occasion from some accidental conversation which happen in the company to write a pleasant definition of a embassador in these word legatus est vir bonus peregre-missus ad mentiendum republicæ causa which he choose should have be thus render into english : a ambassador be a honest man send to lie abroad for the good of he country but the word lie upon which the conceit turn be not so express in latin as to admit a double meaning or so fair a construction as sir henry think in english about eight year after this album fall into the hand of gaspar scioppius a restless zealot who publish book against king jame and upbraid he for entertain such scandalous principle as he embassador have express by that sentence : this aspersion gain ground and it become fashionable in venice to write this definition in several glass window these incident reach the ear of king jame he be much displeased with the behavior of he embassador on that occasion and from a innocent piece of witticism sir henry be like to pay very dear by lose he master 's favor upon this we author write two apology one to velserus which be disperse in germany and italy and another to the king both which be so well write that he majesty upon read they declare that sir henry wotton have sufficiently commutt for a greater offence upon this reconciliation sir henry become more in favor with he majesty than ever like friend who have be for some time separated they meet again with double fervor and they friendship increase to a greater warmth during the twenty year which sir henry be ambassador at venice he have the good fortune to be so well respect by all the duke and the lead man of the republic that he interest every year increase and they seldom deny he any favor he ask for he countryman who come to venice which be as walton express it a city of refuge for all englishman who be any way distressed in that republic walton proceed to relate two particular instance of the generosity and tenderness of he disposition and the nobleness of he mind which as they serve to illustrate he character deserve a place here there have be many englishman bring by commander of they own country to serve the venetian for pay against the turk and those english by irregularity and imprudence commit such offence as bring they into prison and expose they to work in gally wotton could not be a unconcerned spectator of the misery of he countryman : they offence he know proceed rather from wantonness and intemperance than any real principle of dishonor and therefore he think it not beneath he to become a petitioner for they releasement he be happy in a successful representation of they calamity they be set at liberty and have a opportunity of return to they own country in comfort in place of languish in jail and be slave at the gally and by this compassionate interposition with the republick he have the blessing of many miserable wretch : the highest pleasure which any human being can enjoy on this side immortality of the generosity and nobleness of he mind walton give this instance upon sir henry wotton 's come a second time to venice he be employ as embassador to several of the german prince and to the emperor ferdinando ii and this embassy to these prince be to incline they to equitable measure for the restoration of the queen of bohemia and she descendant to they patrimonial inheritance of the palatinate this be by eight month constant endeavor and attendance upon the emperor and he court bring to a probability of a successful conclusion by a treaty but about that time the emperor 's army fight a battle so fortunately as put a end to the expect treaty and sir henry wotton 's hope who when he quit the emperor 's court humbly advise he to use he victory with moderation which advice the emperor be please to hear graciously be well satisfy with wotton 's behavior during he residence at he court he then tell he that tho ' the king he master be look upon as a abetter of he enemy yet he could not help demonstrate he regard to he by make he a present of a rich jewel of diamond worth more than ten thousand pound this be receive with all possible respect by sir henry but the next morning upon he depart from vienna at he take leave of the countess of sabrina a italian lady in whose house he reside he express he gratitude for she civility by present she with the jewel give he by the emperor which be afterwards discover be by the emperor take as a affront but sir henry acknowledge he gratitude for the mark of distinction shewn to he at the same time declare he do not chuse to receive profit from any present give he by a enemy of he royal mistress for so the queen of bohemia the eldest daughter of the king of england permit he to call she upon sir henry wotton 's return from he embassy he signify a inclinacion to the king to be excuse from any further employment in foreign affair to retire from the bustle of life and spend the evening of he day in studious ease and tranquility he majesty in consequence of this request promise he the reversion of a office which be the place of master of the rolle if he out-live sir julius cæsar who then possess it and be grow so old that he be say to be keep alive beyond nature 's course by the prayer of the many people who daily live upon he bounty here it will not be improper to observe that sir henry wotton have thro ' a generosity of temper reduce he affair to such a state that he could not live without some profitable employment as he be indebted to many person for money he borrow to support he dignity in he embassy the king 's appointment for that purpose be either not regularly pay or too inconsiderable for the expence this render it impossible for he to wait the death of sir julius cæsar besides that place have be long sollicit by that worthy gentleman for he son and it would have be think a ill-natured office to have by any means prevent it it luckily happen at this time that the provostship of he majesty 's college at eaton become vacant by the death of mr murray for which there be many earnest and powerful sollicitation this place be admirably suit to the course of life wotton resolve to pursue for the remain part of he day he have see enough of the world to be sick of it and be now three-score year of age he think a college be the fittest place to indulge contemplation and to rest he body and mind after a long struggle on the theater of life in he suit for this place he be happily successful and immediately enter into holy order which be necessary before he could take possession of he new office walton have relate the particular manner of he spend he time which be divide between attendance upon public devotion the more private duty of religion and the care which he function demand from he of the affair of the college in the year 1639 sir henry die in eaton-college and be bury in the chapel belong to it he direct the following sentence to be put upon a marble monument to be erect over he hic jacit hujus sententiæ primus author disputandus pruritus ecclesiarum scabies nomen alias quære which may be thus render into english here lyeth the first author of this sentence the itch of disputation will prove the scab of the church enquire he name elsewhere sir henry wotton have be allow by all critic to be a man of real and great genius a upright statesman a polite courtier compassionate and benevolent to those in distress charitable to the poor and in a word a honest man and a pious christian as a poet he seem to have no considerable genius he versification be harmonious and sometimes have a air of novelty he turn be elegant and he thought have both dignity and propriety to recommend they there be a little piece amongst he collection call the world which we shall quote before we give a account of he work the world 's a bubble : and the life of man less than a span in he conception wretched : from the womb so to the tomb nurst from he cradle and bring up to year with care and fear who then to frail mortality shall trust but lymn in water or but write in dust yet whil ` st with sorrow here we live opprest what life be best court be but only superficial school to dandle fool : the rural part be turn into a den of savage man : and where 's a city from vice so free but may be term the word of all the three domestic care afflict the husband 's bed or pain he head those that live single take it for a curse or do thing worse these would have child those that have they none or wish they go : what be it then to have or have no wife but single thraldom or a double strife we own affection still at home to please be a disease to cross the sea to any foreign soil peril and toil war with they noise father carry he when he be appoint lord deputy of that kingdom in 1622 he have he academical learning in trinity college in dublin and in st john 's college cambridge clarendon relate that before he inactivity of that summer he return to england and apply himself to a severe course of study first to polite literature and poetry in which he make several successful attempt in a very short time he council table when he majesty be present but seem to lord it over all the rest not by the force of argument but a assume superiority to which he have no right this nettled lord falkland and make he hampden 's after much importunity he at last accept the seal of he majesty and serve in that employment with unshaken integrity be above corruption of any kind when he be vest with that high dignity dissimulation of manners wind themselves into such trust and secret as enable they to make discovery neither could he ever suffer himself to open letter upon a suspicion that they might contain matter of dangerous consequence and proper for statesman to know as to the first he condemn they as void of all honor and who ought justly to be abandon to infamy and that no single preservation could be worth so general a wound and corruption of society as encourage such people would carry with it the last he think such a violation of the law of nature that no qualification by office could justify he in the trespass and tho ' the necessity of the time make it clear that those advantage be not to be decline and be necessary to be practice yet he find mean to put it off from himself -lrb- 4 -rrb- the dry wrangling of the law as there have be often instance of poet and man of genius be educate to the law so here it may not be amiss to observe that we remember not to have meet with one amongst they who continue in that profession a circumstance not much in its favor and be a kind of proof that the professor of it be generally compose of man who be capable of application but without genius mr drummond have as we have already observe a sovereign contempt for the law apply himself to the sublimer study of poetry and history in both which he become very eminent have relinquish all thought of the bar or appear in public he retire to he pleasant seat at hawthornden and there by read the greek and latin author enrich the world with the product of he solitary hour after he have recover a very dangerous fit of sickness he write he cypress grove a piece of excellent prose both for the fineness of the stile and the sublimity and piety of the sentiment : in which he represent the vanity and instability of human affair teach a due contempt of the world propose consolation against the fear of death and give we a view of eternal happiness much about this time he write the flower of sion in verse though the number in which these poem be write be not now very fashionable yet the harmony be excellent and during the reign of king jame and charle i we have meet with no poet who seem to he by the earl of norwich while he exercise he function at waltham the archdeacon of norwich engage he to interest himself in favor of the church of wolverhampton from which a patrimony be detain by a prospect of the spanish match on the success of which they build they hope begin to betray a great degree of insolence and proudly boast the pedigree of they church from the apostle themselves they insist that as they church be the first so it be the best and that no ordination be valid which be not derive from it hall in answer to they assertion make a concession which some of he protestant brethren think he have no right to do he acknowledge the priority of the roman church but deny its infallibility and consequently that it be possible another church might be more pure and approach more to the apostolic practice than the romish this controversy he manage so successfully that he be promote to the see of exeter and as king jame i seldom know any bound to he generosity when he most material circumstance the insolence of some churchman and the superiority they assume in the civil government during the distraction of charle i provoke the house of common to take some measure to prevent they grow power which that pious monarch be too much disposed to favor in consequence of this the lead member of the opposition petition the king to remove the bishop from they seat in parliament as illegal upon this principle that as they be part of the legislature no law could pass during they absence at least if that absence be produce by violence which clarendon have fully crashaw son of a eminent divine name william crashaw be educate in grammar learning in sutton 's - hospital call the charter-house near london and in academical partly in pembroke-hall of which he be a scholar and afterwards in peterhouse cambridge of which he be a fellow where as in the former house he be distinguish for he latin and english poetry afterwards he take the degree of master of art but be soon after throw out of he fellowship with many other of the university of cambridge for deny the covenant during the time of the rebellion he be for a time oblige to shift for himself and struggle against want and oppression at length be weary with persecution and poverty and foresee the calamity which threaten and afterwards fall upon he church and country by the unbounded fury of the presbyterian he change he religion and go beyond sea in order to recommend himself to some popish preferment in pari but be a mere scholar be incapable of execute he new plan of a livelihood mr abraham cowley hearing of he be there endeavor to find he out which he do and to he great surprize see he in a very miserable plight : this happen in the year 1646 this generous bard give he all the assistance he could and obtain likewise some relief for he from henrietta marium the queen dowager then reside at paris we author receive letter of recommendation from he queen he take a journey into italy and by virtue of those letter become a secretary to a cardinal at rome and at length one of the canon or chaplain of the rich church of we lady of loretto some mile distant from thence where he die in 1650 this conduct of crashaw can by no means be justify : when a man change one religion for another he ought to do it at a time when no motive of interest can well be suppose to have produce it for it do no honor to religion nor to the person who become a convert when it be evident he would not have alter he opinion have not he party be suffer and what would have become of the church of england what of the protestant religion what of christianity in general have the apostle and primitive martyr and later champion for truth meanly abandon it like crashaw because the hand of power be lift up against it it be a old observation that the blood of the martyr be the seed of the church but crashaw take care that the church mould reap no benefit by he perseverance before he leave england have also write carman deo nostro be hymn and other sacred poem address to the countess of denbigh he be say to have be master of five language besides he mother tongue viz hebrew greek latin italian adieu unkind where still be nothing worth \* \* \* \* \* john ford a gentleman of the middle-temple who write in the reign of charle i he be a well-wisher to the muse and a friend and acquaintance of most of the poet of he time he be not only a partner with rowley and decker in the witch of edmonton and with decker in the sun 's darling but write likewise himself seven play most of which be act at the phænix in the black-fryar and may be know by a anagram instead of he name generally print in the title-page viz fide honor he genius be more turn for tragedy than comedy which occasion a old poet to write thus of he : deep in a dump john ford be alone get with fold arm and melancholy hat these particulars i find in mr langbaine who give the follow account of he play 1 broken heart a tragedy which this author die but imagine from circumstance that it must have be some time before the restoration and before the year 1657 for the sun 's darling write between he and decker be publish in 1657 which mr langbaine say be after they decease \* \* \* \* \* thomas middleton live in the reign of king charle i he be cotemporary with johnson fletcher maslinger and rowley in whose friendship he be say to have share and though he fall much short of the two former yet be join with they in write play he arrive at some reputation he join with fletcher and johnson in a play call the widow and the highest honor that be know of this poet be he be admit to make a triumvirate with two such great man : he join with massinger and rowley in write the old law he be likewise assist by rowley in write
